<Author>Reston10
<Content>Very Good Business Focused Hotel I stayed an entire week at the Hotel Arts for a business meeting. For that purpose, the hotel was very good. If I was visiting Barcelona as a tourist, I would probably look for something a little less sterile. The staff are very attentive and friendly. It's one of those places where the staff won't give you directions to the elevator, but rather they'll walk you there and press the button for you. I arrived at 12:00 noon. There were queen bedded rooms available, but I wanted a king. The hotel called my cellphone around 2:00 to say that a king room was ready. They gave me a corner room that faced the sea. The room was long and narrow. It had a very nice bathroom, a desk that faced the marina, a king-sized bed, and a couple of chairs. The desk wasn't very comfortable for working. The bathroom had a bath with a hand-held shower; a toilet room with toilet and bidet, a shower, and a double-sink. The shower was like a high-pressure car wash. It had a fixture in the ceiling, and then two fixtures on the wall. The wall fixture jets were piercing so I used that only once. There was every sort of imaginable toiletry -- the normal things like shampoo, body wash, bar soap, mouthwash, etc., plus a comb, cotton balls, q-tips, a toothbrush and toothpaste, a razor with shaving cream, a sewing kit, a nail file, etc. The room has a lot of technology. There is a Bang  Olufsen television/stereo system. By today's standards (and considering what they spent on that set-up) the television was small and hard to see from the bed. There was no alarm clock (at least I couldn't figure out where it was). The furnishings were very nice, although I found the bed to be uncomfortable. The windows in the bedroom had shutters and electric blinds that could completely darken the room. The room had pretty much everything you would expect -- hair dryer, in-room safe, iron/ironing board, robes, etc. The minibar was well stocked -- although with not much to eat, and what was there was really pricey. I probably spent about EUR50 and consumed two bottles of water, a shot of vodka, and some crackers. Speaking of pricey, wifi is EUR25/day + tax. That's outrageous. Wifi appeared to be free in one hour increments in the lobby. The room lighting was kind of crazy -- there is a master control by the door and another on the nightstand. The switch labels are such that you can't quite figure out which is which without trying them all. For example, the switch labeled the living room operated the lights at the door; and switch labeled the salon operated the lights in the bedroom. The room was very nice, but the carpet had some dark stains, as did the wallpaper. The windows were dirty, and there was lots of dust. From a location perspective, the views are beautiful -- the sea, the city, the architecture. However, it's a long walk into the old part of town, or to see most of the major Gaudi attractions. The metro is close and taxis are plentiful. The pools appear very attractive, although it was in the 60s while I was there, so I didn't venture out (neither did anyone else it seemed). My room rate included the breakfast buffet. There was a lot of variety and the service was attentive. While I read the news on my cell phone, someone offered me a newspaper. I also partook in drinks in two of the bars. The drinks were expensive (EUR12+), but the service was attentive. The furnishings were comfortable, and it was busy well into the early morning. I also dined in Arola. The service was very good, as was the food. There was live music. All-in-all, the hotel was as I expected. It seems to cater more toward conferences and business meetings. The service is attentive and the staff are helpful, without being snooty. The room rate wasn't that bad (EUR300/night + tax), but I did feel a bit nickel'd and dimed.  
<Date>Nov 5, 2008

<Author>marissa2c
<Content>Not Worth the Money Our stop in Barcelona was going to be part of a 3 week European vacation and we decided to splurge for the Ritz Carlton. You can definitely get a 5 star experience if money is no object and you have low/average expectations.But as someone who stays for free in the biggest suites in Las Vegas and has experienced service at the highest levels, the hotel was nice but definitely not worth the money.The staff was friendly but rather useless. If you pose something to them that they haven't trained for in their employee manual, you can see their head about ready to explode.The prices of the food in the restaurant were about double the prices of the very good quality food you can get outside the hotel. The only food that I ate within the hotel was the breakfast buffet. Very good and high quality but definitely not worth the $50/pp price tag. You can get a very nice eggs/bacon/toast breakfast at the deli next door for about $9 + bev.The area around the hotel is nice. The beach is right behind the hotel about a 5 minute walk and there is a boardwalk with about 5 restaurants along the beach. Across the street there is a mall with a pretty good Chinese restaurant, tapas bar, ice cream stand, mexican and italian restaurants, sandwich shop, and a souvenir shop where we stocked up on soda and waters and a great chicken salad sandwich for $4.There is a Touriste bus stop about 2 minutes from the hotel that will take you to all the sites around the city and will take you to the city center and you can walk down Las Ramblas, the main drag. Definitely worth a stop is the Boqueria which is an open air market and has the freshest and best tasting fruit I've ever had in my life.In summary, the Ritz is a nice hotel, but you'll definitely overpay.

<Author>KSLTowcester
<Content>Not really 5 star Stayed at this hotel for a short break with my 15 year old daughter. Our first meal at the poolside restaurant was very poor quality and mine I returned, whilst the meal we experienced at the Enoteca Restarant left both of us with upset stomachs. The room service was useless, an inability to co-ordinate the coffee facilities so that cups, saucers, milk and teaspoon were all available at the same time prevailed for our entire stay. It took two days and several visits from a rather sweaty and smelly engineer (with very dirty shoes) to get the shower working properly. The in-room toiletries had already been used by a previous guest. The lifts broke (luckily we were only on the 5th floor). One day the room was not made up until just before bedtime and on another day it was not made up at all. The final ineptitude was the staff managing to lose our suitcases between the reception area and the taxi area as we were leaving which resulted in our having to rummage around the hotel baggage store.We did speak with the hotel duty manager on our final night and he was kind enough to reimburse us the cost of the Enoteca dinner, give us a further small discount and offer us the use of our room until 4pm on the day of our departure. However the shambles continued even after that conversation and we left after what should have been a relaxing stay at a luxury hotel, rather stressed and relieved to be leaving.It was not a five star experience and certainly not one that I could recommend to others.

<Author>EuroLondon
<Content>Pretty great, bit tacky Stayed here in August, on holiday in a standard deluxe room. Paid 鈧?45 for room and breakfast.This is a pretty nice hotel, as I guess you'd expect. The lobby is on the first floor, which is a good safety measure, I think. D茅cor is kind of neutral and expensive-looking - lots of beige, grey, cream etc. Some parts of the hotel are showing minor signs of wear and tear - e.g. carpets - but very minor. Check in was fine - arrived about noon and they were able to give us our room straight away. Reasonably high - 14th floor, with decent views of the beach. I did notice later that some of the rooms on the (I think) 2nd floor seemed kind of dark, with windows looking out onto the rear of the pool-level caf茅- I'd try to avoid them if I were you. Great BO sound system and LCD TV in the room. Also a Nespresso machine, but the hotel charges 鈧? per capsule, which is kind of crazy. I know it's a top-end hotel, and you expect to pay more etc, but 鈧??! That's a markup of around 1300%. Watch out for the 鈧?5 CDs too. Very comfortable beds, great linens and towels. Large bathroom with separate shower cubicle and toilet cubicle. Breakfast was pretty good - standard hotel buffet in the ground floor restaurant. No eggs cooked to order though, for any egg fans out there.A lot of people have noted that the hotel isn't in the centre of town, but it's only a short taxi ride away. It's within walking distance of the Museum of Catalonia and the Maremagnum shopping mall, though. Both are pretty rubbish, actually, so don't be too upset if you don't include them on your itinerary. The museum has the worst rooftop caf茅 - recommended in the Time Out Barcelona Guide - very unfriendly service and poor aircon, so very hot. The Maremagnum mall has very few shops, and of those there are very few you'd actually like to buy things from.The pool was great - decent enough size, not massive though. A lot of children and families around - more than I had anticipated. Lots of attendants to help you find a lounger etc. Plenty of little Spawn of Satans running around, belly flopping and splashing. Tended to get busy by late morning, all the way through to mid-late afternoon. August is very hot, so there's not much point going out until later, I guess.Although it's a very nice hotel, it's got a sort of tacky/trashy feeling at times. It's built on top of something called Casin-Oh! and the whole Olympic Port area is a bit cheesy - a lot of naff-looking bars and restaurants around and underneath. That said, we did eat at one place - Bestial - which was very nice. Guests at the hotel are a mixture of Europeans (Italians, French, Germans - some topless by the hotel pool, watch out), and the stereotypical well-preserved cruise ship guests waiting to embark or having just disembarked. A lot of tight faces wearing sunglasses to breakfast (indoors as well as outdoors) - you get the picture.

<Author>Annie92
<Content>Very nice This is a beautiful hotel in a location we liked a lot - some complain that it is a bit removed from the center of things, but for us this was a positive, and cabs are easy and relatively inexpensive since most everything in Barcelona is quite close. The rooms were very large with great views of the city and beach. We appreciated the light and openness, as compared to most standard European hotels. We had a club room and the lounge and food offerings were excellent. So, in terms of the room, comfort and location the hotel is highly recommended. However, as other reviews have mentioned, the service was not up to par for a hotel of this caliber. I will say that most everyone we encountered was very nice and appeared to at least try, but...for example, we had connecting rooms with the rest of our family and it took two hours (several phone calls, plus my husband going down to reception twice), before someone finally showed up with a shrug to unlock the doors between the two rooms. On several occasions when calling the front desk or operator the phone would ring endlessly with no one ever answering. We were not there for the pool really, but it is very small for a hotel of this size and the couple of times we walked by it was very crowded. A few times we overheard very angry guests who had arranged for things that were not done properly (one person was left at the airport without the ride the hotel was to have arranged for her). For our purposes, we were very pleased with the comfort of the hotel and it was just for a couple of nights. But, if you are looking for someplace with great service that you can depend on, not sure if this is the place.

<Author>Mandy007
<Content>High tech nice hotel We stayed here for 2 nights waiting for our cruise ship embarkation. The lobby is pretty and the room (deluxe double) had a nice view of the beach, was very high tech with automatic blinds, music throughout the room and a beautiful modern bathroom. Decor was neutral, and attractive. We arrived from the airport at 10 in the morning and had to wait until 3:00 for our room to be ready. This is our only complaint. Eventhough check out was noon. They had a nice welcome lounge with free food and drinks and we were given a nice tour of the amazing spa (didn't use it) and access to the pool and changerooms. The art/sculptures throughout were attractive. We paid less than 300 euros/night for the room which was reasonable. There was one 15 metre pool (nice large hammocks and loung chairs surrounding it) as well as a smaller almost like a wading pool. The atmosphere was relaxing with green apples and bottles of water available at the pool. We had to wait for a lounge chair in the shade one day. The food was excellent especially the buffet breakfast. Nicely presented and huge selection including asian choices for breakfast. It was near the beach and many restaurants and not too far from shopping (short taxi ride). Staff were very helpful although the front desk was a little snooty. The concierge were helpful in suggesting restaurants and calling for us. They have greeters who show you to your room and how to use things in your room. It was a nice touch. We enjoyed ourselves and if we went to Barcelona again we would stay here.

<Author>TwoHavlesofCoconuts
<Content>5 star room, 3 star service and pool My wife and I stayed at the Arts for vacation. The room was very nice and very clean. 5 star room by US standards. The food at the restaurants was very good, but not excellent, and very expensive. The wine selection is very large. The staff at the restaurants however, were superb. The hotel staff on the other hand missed the mark. Here is where the hotel lets you down. I asked for two types of pillows in the online request. The front desk receptionist confirmed my request. When we got to the room we found the request not met. I had trouble working the phone (I don't know if it was me or the phone). I called for help 4 times and each time I was told help was on the way. No help arrived. I requested a birthday cake for my wife to be delievered at a particular time in writing and recieved confirmation in writing. The cake was not delivered on time. It took a lot of work to get it sorted out. I made a reservation at one of the restaurants in writing and recieved confirmation in writing. When we arrived at the restaurant, they had no record of the reservation. When I needed help printing a boarding pass the floor attendant was worthless and gave me the wrong information. Another issue was the pool. There is only one pool which is outdoors. The pool was icy cold so if you go at a time other than high season, you may be in for a shock. The view from the pool is poor. The pool is small and there is not enough lounge chairs. Bar service ends at 5pm (I think) or at least way before I thought it should. There is a casino next door which brought in some guests you would not normally have at such a hotel. Reminded me of a sceen out of the movie Swingers. The crowd around the casino is a bit annoying outside as well.The hotel is not on the beach, but very close and the closest I saw (about 100 yards). All and all, I would not stay there again because the hotel simply lacked the service one expects with a 5 star hotel and particularly when you are paying 5 star prices.However, if service is not important and all you want is a 5 star room close to the beach, then I would recommend it.

<Author>qegsbabe
<Content>5* hotel 5* prices Recently spent my 20th wedding anniversary here so paid more than normal for a high hotel room with a sea view, having said that despite the special request made some time ago and arriving mid afternoon we weren't as high as I hoped and the bed arrangement for a sea view had to be 2 queens not a king so rooms are very obviously allocated on arrival and sometimes you are lucky and get an upgrade and sometimes, like us, you have to get what you are given. No attention was paid to the point made prior that it was our wedding anniversary, at these prices I expected a complimentary bottle of wine or box of chocolates but not to be. Having said all that the hotel was gorgeous (the weather helped after arriving from rain in the UK). The staff were helpful and sitting in the lobby as we did watching the beautiful people glide in and out we were frequently offered complimentary water, the pool area although small was well organised with staff attentive to getting sunbeds, free water and apples, even offering to spray the suntan lotion! it is a good 20-30 walk along busy roads from the main shopping etc but overlooked the beach and sea so you it felt more of a holiday than a city break and the taxi was very cheap. Local to the hotel was the lovely port surrounded by numerous reasonably priced bars etc so we never ate in the hotel, not even breakfast, the deli cafe round the corner was excellent for coffee and croissants. The shock was the drink prices, a beer around the pool was 12 euros so all our drinking was done outside because the prices just seemed immoral which was a shame because the hotel had some beautiful bar areas. if money was no object I would definately stay again but younger people might want to be more in the thick of the action.

<Author>Gustavas
<Content>The Ritz Carlton of Barcelona THE ARTS HOTEL, BARCELONAThe Arts Hotel is a Ritz Carlton property directly on the Mediterranean that stands like a monument to modern luxury. High tech and chic, this hotel is stunning in a multitude of ways. Uniformed, professional courtesy and meticulous attention to detail reside in every square foot of this marble and glass masterpiece. The men and women working there all look like Vogue ads or GQ models but act like true professionals. The service, amenities, attitude and property are all truly first class with no exceptions. The high-rise suites (we were on the 28th floor) are phenomenal, extra huge and very pricey with sweeping views of the city and the sea. A large living room, two TV鈥檚, dressing room, two separate bathrooms, a wide hallway leading to a massive corner view bedroom, a full bar and more high tech buttons than anyone requires. From the marble and polished granite master bathroom (you could park a car in this one with plenty of space to spare) to the mood lighting and push button electronic curtains and drapes that covered the massive floor to ceiling windows, these suites and this hotel will definitely please. I was informed by pool attendant and the bellman that several film stars request this suite as well. We decided to enjoy a little pool side time and then the beach before a late afternoon nap and ultimately, dinner. The pool here is five star. Attendants escort guests to their choice of designer lounge seating and welcome you with several lush towels, designer umbrellas and bottles of water. On the beach however, don鈥檛 be surprised to see several topless bathers. With the horrible value of the dollar in Europe, cash goes quickly here also. Two cocktails at pool side amounted to a U.S. conversion of $56.00. It鈥檚 all relative when one considers that a suite at the Arts Hotel runs $1000 a night, plus, plus. Later that evening, while enjoying a state of the art shower system than can best be described as a private cocoon of marble with multiple and powerful water jets, (LBJ would have loved it) we were getting prepared for our evening on the town before the cruise the following day. We had reservations for a late dinner that night as we enjoyed the glittering lights of Barcelona from 28 floors beneath us. While getting ready, the extensive surround stereo sound system (even in the bathroom) lulled us with Andre Bocelli from CD鈥檚 provided ensuite. The concierge desk rang politely to tell us that our driver was downstairs and ready when we were. There were frequently so many black and midnight blue Mercedes S-Class sedans with suited drivers waiting outside this hotel that you鈥檇 think it was a diplomatic location. Admittedly, being driven around Barcelona in this manner is a great convenience and goes hand in hand with the culture of this hotel.After a 20 minute ride past the Ramblas into the buzz, sights and nightlife of downtown Barcelona, we arrived at a well established and popular restaurant called Botafumiero. A busy, elegant, old world seafood paradise. Reservations a must. Passing wall photos of famous former diners including politicians and actors, we were greeted warmly and escorted to our table. I had noticed that among the photos were Bill Clinton, Robert De Niro, Cuba Gooding and even King Juan Carlos and Queen Sophia posing with the owner. Apparently the Spanish royal family keeps a place in Barcelona and eat at Botafumiero. In a word, excellent. Had a wonderful shellfish broth, a great Cabernet and the Mediterranean sea bass. Slightly brisk but professional service with truly fabulous food. Highly recommended. Later we were driven around the sights and ended our evening at the large and busy casino next door to the hotel. The following morning we indulged in a memorably delicious breakfast amidst the gentle sea breeze surrounded by lush floral gardens and delightful service at the garden terrace of the hotel. This is one of many beautiful locations to eat at this hotel. In a matter of a few hour it was time to embark the Oceania Insignia for our Med voyage. Checkout was seamless and with our car and driver at the ready, we were off to the pier terminal for our Mediterranean cruise. The Arts is a stellar hotel with stellar service.

<Author>ChicagoFrank
<Content>Excellent concierge service Stayed at the Arts with my wife for 3 nights and all I can say is it was a bliss! Rooms are very large for european standards, astonishing views of the Gaudi church from our 22nd floor and very comfortable bed. Concierge service is the best I have ever experienced. Delta lost our bags and Mery was extremely helpful and kept us updated. After several calls we had our luggage sent to the hotel, which was a relief! Carlos was also terrific and his restaurant recommendations were great. We were booked at Enoteca and Botafumero. He also arranged tickets for Palaue, which is a beautiful opera hall. They both remembered our names during our stay and made us feel like celebrities. On our last day we decided to take a train to Sitges for a getaway and it was really nice. I have always believed that concierge service makes the difference between a good and an excellent hotel and Hotel Arts concierge is definitely outstanding. I would strongly recommend this hotel to anyone visiting Barcelona.

<Author>JonnySLondon
<Content>Very, very Stylish. But you do pay for it.If value-for-money is important to you, then you shouldn't be looking at this hotel.We stayed in a club level room, and it was sumptuous. We have stayed in some nice places over the years and I don't ever recall my wife looking so impressed at the standard of the room as she did here.The bed was so comfortable.The bathroom was very smart, dual sinks in the middle - one side had a separate room for the toilet and bidet, and a separate wet room for the shower. The other side had a recess with the bath in it. My wife now wants the same arrangement at home.....Staying at the club level gives you access to the club lounge. They have five different buffet spreads on per day, nothing substantial, but enough so that you don't need to eat elsewhere if you don't want to. Plus there seems to be an endless supply of champagne.The service in the club lounge is very attentive, but not intrusive.It was unfortunate that we were in Barcelona for the heaviest rain that they have ever known, and the hotel was not geared up for it. Water was leaking into the club lounge. As a result of the leaks into other parts of the hotel they had to turn the water to the rooms off for most of Saturday afternoon / evening while repairs were conducted. This was incredibly inconvenient if you were there at the time but I doubt that that is a regular occurrence.The location is a bit far from the centre of town, it is at the very boundary of walkable, and that is only if you have a lot of energy. There is a metro station nearby though, and the concierge at the entrance have a button for summoning taxis.As for the noise, we were on the 30th floor and from there we could hear the sirens of emergency vehicles, and the whistle of the policeman directing traffic outside, but not too much else.In summary, I would only recommend this place if you want to spend a load of money on a treat.You can expect to see some celebrities while you are there too.

<Author>Flunie
<Content>Beautiful but watch your wallet My wife and I just spent 4 nights at the Hotel Arts in Barcelona as part of a corporate conference. At first I was uncertain about the location, being next to the pier and Marina as opposed to the centre o ftown. However, it turned out to actually be a plus, since the weather was gorgeous and it was really a pleasure having access to the pool, beach and pier. Getting to and from the city centre was never a problem, either by taxi or subway. I would say, though it麓s key to get a room with a sea view. Apparently there is construction and scaffolding for all rooms below the 8th floor, and we complained at the front desk so a very nice young man upgraded us to the 9th floor with a beautiful sea view. The room was very nice, not huge, but with a large bathroom and one of the best showers I麓ve had. In general, the hotel was great. Very nicely designed, great food and excellent service with terrific concierges. BUT, it麓s a good thing our company was paying the bill since prices were outrageous. We were charged 18 Euros for a sangria in the bar, and my wife was going to have her hair done in the salon before a black tie dinner until she learned it was 120 Euros. Outrageous. The only other thing to mention is that the hotel was very busy and noisy, perhaps due to a long holiday weekend in Barcelona. Finally, out of our group of about 65 couples, 5 or 6 people were either pickpocketed or had purses, cellphones, bags stolen from them, 2 incidents happened in the hotel. Although the hotel dealt with it quickly and sympathetically, you got the feeling this was extremely commonplace. It麓s a real shame that people had their trips ruined like this. I can麓t believe why such a beautiful city and country can麓t do something to better protect its tourists.So, enjoy Hotel Arts and Barcelona, but watch your wallet on both counts.

<Author>SentosaDubai_UAE
<Content>Arts for Arts sake!! Difficult to start the review for this particular hotel. The arrival and greeting on formal name terms is endearing and the friendliness of staff genuine almost relaxing after a long journey. Reception is a dream area with the abundance of fresh flora and fauna. I stayed in room 1414 with sea and city views. It was pretty noisy being next to a casino and lots of sirens from police and ambulances all night. The room though was just a perfect size and one of the most comfortable I have stayed in. Bang Olufson sounds and TV were superb and bathrooms divine. Now the downside of the place. The mini-bar prices are totally outrageous and the most expensive I have ever seen. A beautiful coffee machine was there, work of art but users beware that each and every tiny sachet you use is 4 Euros, each small bottle of water is 5 Euros and each can of Coke 7 Euros, totally outrageous on the VERY expensive rates they charge for the room. Breakfast runs at 30 Euros per person and BEWARE they have IVA (VAT) on everything! So if you want luxury it comes at a cost and this place costs., believe me! At the rate they charge free bottled water and free tea/coffee would be small change for the hotel. The Six Senses Spa on the top floors again is a 40 Euro entrance and includes no extra treatments. The booklet they leave in your room has no price list which begs to make one think if you need to know the price its too expensive for you? To eat in the hotel or use the bar well be ready for really high prices, but fantastic presentation. The area around the hotel has pleanty of excellent local restaurants and bars with great atmosphere, The Agua restaurant was fantastic food and ambiance. Barcelona is a great place and really upcoming. They profess that the Rolling Stones stayed here. Might be nice to see a TA Report from Mick or Keith ..??? To me though the Arts hotel is more business like than leisure but who knows I may return, never say never! Happy travels! Ciao

<Author>AAflyerSeattle
<Content>Cool Hotel in Barcelona A beautiful and modern hotel in Barcelona. The things we loved included, our beautiful room with very modern features, flat screen TV, large bathroom, with a wonderful, large shower. Shower had multiple shower heads which is rare in most hotels. There was a great coffee machine in our room..we made espresso each morning. The privacy screen completely blocked any light coming into the room. Definitely ask for a wake up call. Staff was super friendly and helpful. Most spoke perfect English. We had a King size bed and it was super comfortable. Some comments for anyone considering visiting Barcelona and this hotel: I definitely want to comment on the pick pockets..it is a big problem and happened to one of our friends on the same trip. Watch your wallet and purse, no matter where you are. There is a casino next door and on the Friday night, we could hear the disco music until 3 am in the morning, so I would book on a higher floor next time. There is some traffic noise, but not terrible. Breakfast buffet at the hotel is great. Also ate at their small snack restaurant, I think called Bites and it was just ok. But with plenty of restaurants in the city, this wasn't a big deal. Finally, you do need to take a Metro or cab for shopping in the old section of town. If this is important, I would stay closer to Las Ramblas.

<Author>misstee
<Content>Out of this world, felt like being in a James Bond movie!! I was fortunate enough to stay at this hotel for a mere 3nights on part of our honeymoon. All I can say is I cannot believe there are any bad reviews for this place, it was so utterly beautiful. We were very lucky, booked with expedia, got a great rate, just a normal room, but I mentioned in the request box that it was our honeymoon, and any extras would be welcome!. It was with disbelief that when we checked in, the lady on the front desk took us into the lift ,and showed us how to insert our special key, to get to the 2 top floors, as we had been upgraded to an exclusive room on the top 2 floors, which only the lucky few, very rich, had access to. There was a special lounge on this floor, with 360 degree views and free drinks and food whenever you wanted! We had champagne and chocolate dipped strawberries just before we went out for the evening, and I felt like I was in a James Bond Movie. The skyline looks so gorgeous at night, and the hotel staff just make you feel as though you've won the lottery!! The room was a corner room and had floor to ceiling glass windows,all the way around, with a small lounge area, large bathroom with double shower wet room, bath, and every gadget you could think of. We could lie in our fabulous, sumptuous beds, and using a remote control, bring down electronic shutters to all the windows! They even had their own cd called Barcelona Nights for you to play! The sound system was excellent. The view from the room was just incredible at night. I was very impressed with the design, and detail of everything, and the service, and breakfast were excellent. The outdoor swimming pool was surrounded by double-bed sun loungers, with thick mattresses., which I thought was a lovely thought- free fruit and iced water, towels, were all waiting for you. It is true though that it was a little noisy with traffic, as you are not that far from the roads, although you can't see them, (you are kind of, underneath the incredible big bronze statue. )But you can't really complain, as you are in the centre of Barcelona and I think it kind of added to the excitement of the city! The beach is only a short walk over the busy road, and is lovely soft sand, but no shade (atificial beach but you couldn't tell! )so watch out! We were also able to walk to restaurants in the evening. Just a tip to say that we took an open top bus tour which was a great way to see everything, but I was devasted to find that when we arrived to go around gaudi's palace, they only accept cash at the entrance, and we had missed all banks as they all shut for siesta around 2.30pm and hubby forgot pin!!. So we have an excuse to go back!! I truely hope so!! To sum it up, total luxury, will greatly appeal to people who appreciate art and culture, or want something extra special, quality and service. Not a place to take young kids though, its just too posh!

<Content>Amazing views, amazing hotel I've now stayed here 3 times and it's always been a pleasure.The first time I came here, we were upgraded and had access to El Club, with free food and drink on tap any time. That was brilliant, but the clubhouse itself was inhabited by bored American teenagers who spent most of the time sulking because the hotel's policy means they won't serve alcohol to under 21s. We noticed that the sand in the ashtrays by the lift (this is Spain after all, where smoking is a national pastime) were stamped with the hotel's logo. As a test of the hotel's service standards, we dibbled in the sand and timed how long it took for someone to come around and re-stamp it. Not that long, as it turns out.

<Author>csattsjr
<Content>Great hotel, little busy The Hotel Arts is a beautiful, very modern hotel located on the beach in Barcelona. I was a little disappointed as the hotel was extremely busy, and it changed the whole ambiance of the hotel. You could not walk anywhere without there being at least 30 people surrounding you. Additionally, the elevators were very inefficient, often skipping floors. We actually stood in line for an elevator for 20 minutes. For a high rise (about 42 floors) building, I expected a little bit more efficiency. The spa was to die for, the views were amazing and the relaxation room you are taken to after your treatment has 6 beds where you can choose to nap or relax. The club floors came with great amenities and my glass was always full of champagne as they never let my glass remain empty for too long. One other complaint, the maids smoked cigarettes continuously in their quarters, which happened to be right outside our room, so the hallway always stunk of cigarette smoke. Overall, beautiful hotel, great location next to the marina and amazing views.

<Author>SeasonedTraveler73
<Content>I've stayed at much nicer hotels... Everything from unseasoned staff to lack of cleaniness made our stay less than impressive. This hotel has seen better days. The decor was ok, it reminded me of the W in San Fran, but without artwork in the rooms and other little touchs...in fact the furniture was beat-up and worn-out. The shower, which I'm sure was nice when it was new, was gross and was in serious need of bleaching...I don't care for bathing in a moldy shower (something I would expect from a lower tier hotel perhaps). During our seven day stay the floor in the bathroom was never cleaned. We had an incident where the staff enter our room while we had the privacy light on and when we questioned it, the front desk stated they were having difficulities with their system and perhaps we didn't leave the red light on...which was not true, we we returned to our room the staff person was in our room and the do not distrub light was clearly on. We inquired about a private tour around Barcelona and were given a brochure for a bus tour - hmmm, I believe they missed the boat on who their target audience appears to be. They also directed us to a closed train station...it appears the rest of Barcelona knew the station was closed for repairs. Another stunning display of customer care was when my husband and I left early to go sight seeing. On our way out of the room, my husband mentioned to me that we were out of toilet paper, we agreed that there was no need to call and request more as this would be taken care when the staff came to clean the room. Upon returning later than evening, we were welcomed to a room with no toilet paper...I guess the cleaning staff and turn-down service were out of it each time the tended to our room. When I called to request a new roll, it took them over 30 minutes to bring us new ones...I wish I was joking. Later in the week we requested two extra pillows and that took over an hour and two calls to be delivered. Interestingly enough, we had just spent the previous week at a Marriot in Vienna were the service was incredible and the room was clean! If you are looking for Ritz Carlton service, I would not recommend Hotel Arts...they truly don't match the stays I've had in Maui or Palm Beach.

<Author>clieves
<Content>Beautiful Hotel My wife and I stayed at the Arts for 3 nights in a club room. The hotel is very stylish with beautiful interiors and stunning flower and fruit arrangements throughout. The bedroom was very spacious and stylishly furnished with a huge bed and fabulous linens. There was also a fantastic Bang  Olufsen flat screen TV and sound system. The bathrooms are very smart with separate WC and huge walk in shower as well as 2 basins and a bath. Massive white towels, everything you would expect from a deluxe hotel. Most criticism on the site seems to be about the level of service. Here are some of our experiences, the hotel pre booked all our dinner reservations prior to our arrival at some of the city鈥檚 top restaurants. The night we arrived we had to change plans on an ongoing basis as my wife鈥檚 flight was severely delayed (we were travelling from different cities) meaning our original dinner plans had to be abandoned. The girls in the club lounge looked after all of this (whilst I was reading a book and enjoying a free glass of wine or two!) and when my wife finally arrived Bites had been kept open so that we could eat there. The service was perfect and for people who complain about the price of everything, I do not think Euro90 over the top for two main courses, a bottle or wine, a couple of bottles of water and coffees. These are normal deluxe hotel charges. The following morning we were greeted in the lounge by name and enjoyed a very pleasant breakfast. After a day鈥檚 sightseeing we again used the lounge facilities pre dinner. A well stocked bar and different types of food depending on the time of day are always available. The lounge staff worked out which bars in the city would be showing the rugby world cup semi finals for us to watch on the Saturday and generally helped whenever they could. The level of service continued like this throughout.That is about all really apart from the say the longest we waited for a lift was one minute and our room was on the 32nd floor.

The design of the hotel, the rooms are holding up amazingly well, the food is very good, the conciege very good and the location is nice. <Author>goodmannersUk
<Content>Beautiful hotel but beware of groups We stayed from 23/08 until 29/08. Having read some of the reviews we were a little apprehensive about staying - would we get a good room, etc. We were given a stunning room on the 27th floor with a view of the city and the beach. The hotel is truly beautiful and as it was summer we took great advantage of the pool and jacuzzi. Except for the last day, we had a good time. The only downfalls were: a lot of very bad mannered teenagers use the jacuzzi and ate ice cream in the tub with the consequence that a lot of empty glassware was left around the side. Also the children placed serviettes and plastic cups in the water. Apart from this, the staff were very helpful and the hotel kept very clean. Our last day was spoilt due to a group, MetLife, reserving at the last moment the whole of the hotel - consequently the pool was closed at 6pm (very early for summer) with very little notice (the notice didn't go up until 10am that day) and some of the staff from the group not very polite as they were already milling around guests trying to relax. Several other guests complained as well but as the hotel was short of staff, some of these were placed to assist the group and as a result the service went down a little. I would still highly recommend the hotel despite this disappointment but would strongly advise you to find out if other groups are booked at the same time or not. Groups need to understand that individual guests go to the hotel to relax and not be stressed out by so many people milling around and as it was our wedding anniversary we felt doubly cheated that day.

<Author>travel_addict14
<Content>nice rooms, extras way overpriced (here is a sample price list!) Giving it 3 stars, because for a 5 star property, the hotel did not live up to expectations. The rooms are wonderful (5 stars), the staff OK (4 stars), the restaurants I would not recommned (1 or 2 stars). When I plan trips, I am always wondering what the extras cost at the hotel, so here are a few prices for you so that you can better plan your budget/trip. 50 minute massage = 120 Euros + 16% tax50 minute facial = 115 Euros + 16% taxCoke from mini bar = 7 euros + 7% taxWater from mini bar = 6-8 euros + 7% taxCup of coffee in room = 4 Euross + 7% tax (No, the coffee is not free!!!)Room service breakfast = 29-35 euros + 6 euro delivery charge + 7% tax.Room service sandwich = 22-24 euros + 6 euro delivery charge + 7% taxOK, you get the idea! To get a sense of what things cost outside the hotel, a coffee and croissont at the cafe outside the hotel was 2.4 euros and large bottle of water usually costs 1.5 o3 2 euros. A bottle of coke was 1.40 euros. A sandwhich is between 3-6 euros usually. I would mind paying so much at Hotel Arts if I felt like the quality and service met the prices, but sadly it didn't (I could even eat my main course at the Marina Bar restaurant, it was so bland and tasteless and my friend hated his appetizer and could not eat it)Also, while the hotel is near the beach, it is a bit away from the other sites. A taxi to La Ribera/El Born (great bars and restaurants) is about 5 or 6 euros, about 7-10 to Las Ramblas. The metro is 2 short blocks from the hotel, so I used that a lot.

<Author>bhackehs
<Content>A Very Average Stay - Overstressed Visit After our recent trip to Valencia down the coast from Barcelona, we decided to take a visit to Barcelona and to stay at the Hotel Arts. It was a modern-luxury hotel, which was fine, but the hotel and the conferences they hosted were out of control and mis-managed.Note About Our Stay: A MASSIVE business conference was going on in the hotel. The attendees were extremely rude, all yelling on their cell phones, conducting meetings in the hallway and elevators, and from what numerous staff had told us, many weren鈥檛 even staying at the hotel, but were taking up pool chairs and all the seats at the restaurants, which made all the paying customers extremely angry.The Hotel: The 42 story tower was built in occasion for the 1992 Barcelona Olympic games, and with its sister, are arguably the most visible landmarks in Barcelona. Entering the hotel from a busy street, the porte-cochere had fountains and waterfalls on the right hand side, with a small lobby, with a decadent food store there. Lobby: Going up the elevator to the main lobby, the doors open and we cant even see the floor because of all the bankers and the girls sending them off to their next appointment. However, check-in was fast and easy, with a personal tour of the property with the check-in manager. The lobby, from what I could see, was nicely laid out, with check-in and concierge in the front, with some deep seating toward the back.Room: Taking the elevator up to the 27th floor, we arrived on our floor and to our room overlooking some beaches, the port, the old city, and Montjuic; a very pretty view! In exploring my room, we noticed all of the high-tech touches of the room. Everything electrical in the room can be controlled from the bedside and door side console. The room was of average size and average furniture for a Ritz, but one special thing was a seating area near the panoramic window, which had a heavy lowering shade to keep out the sun and sounds. The bed was very comfortable and had very nice sheets. The bathroom was huge with a separate bath, separate bidet and toilet, and a great separate shower. Very nice indeed.Fitness Center and Spa: The fitness center is located on a lower part of the hotel, after a tricky trek. I never used the fitness center, but saw it, and it looked of a relatively small size for the hotel. However the Spa is located on the top three floors of the hotel, and is brought to us by The Six Senses Group. In a tour of the Spa, a very nice locker room and relaxation area with steam rooms and balconies overlooking the Mediterranean. I imagine it was very nice, and a plus, rarely had any conference attendees.Dining: We dined only at the restaurant off the lobby, because we could never find a seat at a restaurant at the hotel. The restaurant was nice, again the work staff was very short of people, but the food quality was very nice and tasty. Tip: the shops at the Port Olimpic (right next to the hotel) are extremely nice to dine at and are a great way to see some of Barcelona.Cost: For the cost we paid, I should have known something was going on, for a high-200 price for a deluxe room, which seemed to good to be true for a Ritz, and now I see why. Otherwise, like everything else now-a-days, most food were in the high 20 euros. Service: This is the only thing that would bring me back to the hotel. During our stay, we met the Director of Rooms, Sandra, and she was very gracious, insisting to meet us and get our input on the conference situation. She further assured us that the hotel has not invited back many of the conferences for next year for the reason many other reviewers have noticed. Very similarly, Stephanie at the front was very assisting to our stay. This would be one of the only reasons I would return.Overall: A very average stay, while we had some horrible times, we also had some great times and were treated with decency by many people of the staff, who were visibly tired from the conference, looking like many of the over-worked and yelled at airline employees. Now I feel their pain. The service and the rooms would be the only reason I would return. It is very different than many Ritz-Carlton's.

<Author>Karen1769
<Content>Arts Lovely Hotel But Service Disappointing Spent last weekend at the Arts Hotel for a special occasion. For a deluxe 5 star hotel, I was disappointed at the service.When I arrived, the conceirge took my travel case for me which would be delivered to my room after check-in. However, an hour later and a telephone call to the conceirge desk, my case arrived. I just wanted to throw on a bikini and grab my suntan lotion!For the both days I was there, I had to call housekeeping to come and clean my room. On the first day, after spending a busy day, I just wanted to jump in the shower. When I returned back to the room, all the towels had been left on a pile on the floor and the room remained untouched. Needless to say, a maid did come to the room after I had been told that they were busy doing turndown for the evening. I just wanted some fresh towels nevermind about turndown!!. That evening we asked the conceirge to make a dinner reservation for that evening and also one for the Sunday evening as it was a special occasion. On the Sunday, we didn't have a clue where we were going so asked the conceirge desk, which restaurant we had been booked into only to find to our dismay, that nothing had been booked. The lady on the desk then started to ring some restaurants only to find them booked (no surprises at such short notice). By the third restaurant she had called, it was then discovered that a reservation had indeed been made for us but the lady who handled our request the previous evening had failed to tell anyone about it. On returning back to our room after the fiasco with the restaurant reservation, the room had not been cleaned again. Once I can let it go but for a second time, I was annoyed as hell only to be asked that was I sure that I left the light on the door for the room to be cleaned. For those who haven't stayed at Arts before, they do have a simple system. By inside of the door, there are two switches - one to clean the room, one for privacy. Not rocket science but when I complained to the check-out desk that all was not well with our stay, I was told that the switches can be confusing!!Our room was on the 6th floor which you could hear a lot of traffic noise - probably not a problem if your room was higher up.That being said, the rooms are fab, the spa is good with great views from the 43rd floor but expensive. The service round the swimming pool is good. Remember to take ID if you go to the casino next doorIts a real shame that we had the problems that we did otherwise probably couldn't fault the hotel but for the money we paid and the reputation of this hotel, it was rather disappointing.

<Author>PSTravelingMan
<Content>Major 5 Star Hotel that just doesn't hit the mark This is a nice, 5-star hotel in Barcelona that tries very hard but just doesn't quite hit the mark. My friend and I checked into the hotel at two separate times and had two different check-in experiences. Mine was friendly and helpful and even a glass of champagne. His was awkward, his room wasn't ready, no champagne offered and he was getting a suite while I just reserved a regular room. The hotel is large (44 stories) and modern with great views of the city of Barcelona and/or the Mediterranean Sea. The rooms are fairly large, modern and comfortable. The staff was fairly helpful although when my friend arrived by taxi he was not offered help with his two large bags and had to take them to his room by himself. We were both bothered by the housekeeping staff on more than one occassion when we had the do not disturb sign out. Its a great hotel but just doesn't quite live up to the five star reputation it has especially for the price of rooms.

<Author>hobbesmanc
<Content>spectacular choice We have just returned from a wonderful spring bank holiday staying at the Arts.Maybe we were lucky because the hotel wasn't that busy but we had an amazing stay and were treated like royalty by all the staff we encountered. From the limo pick-up at the airport to the final check-out all the staff were super friendly and professional throughout.The location is a bit away from the traditional Barcalona sights but they are easly reachable by taxi in 5 mins or a shortish walk but there are attractions around the beaches and marina themselves including some great restaurants and bars.The hotel architecture is quite brutally modern but the post-industrial chic of the exterior is softened inside by stunning fresh flowers, copious amounts of art and lots of water features. Our room on the 26th floor had amazing views over the Med and was furnished in a cool, contempory way. The bathroom was great with the best power shower I have used.Breakfast outside was a simple but high quality buffet although there was a shockingly priced a la carte menu. As usual in Spain the bacon was crap and the toaster pathetic though!! For this level of service and price though it would have been nice to have eggs/omlettes etc made fresh.The pool area was great with the most fabulous two people hammocks to slumber in the sun whilst the gorgeous staff all in black bring you chilled lime sodas and fresh fruit.Great experience. The only problem was that we loved the hotel so much that we really didn't get to see a lot of the city!

<Content>Great showers, nice room, average hotel We stayed at the Arts for a long weekend having attended a conference at the hotel.Rooms are wonderful - large, well finished with the usual extras (BO TVs, etc) and they have particularly nice the bathrooms - the shower was one of the best I have had in a hotel - really excellent.However the hotel has a peculiar layout and the reception and public areas felt cramped. If you want to see the sights and sounds of Barcelona there are more central hotels.

<Author>MalachiWilliams
<Content>Poor service, but a good hotel Just came back from a three nigh stay at Arts. The room are excellent and I love the bathrooms. My only complaint in the room was the tea and coffee making service. There were no prices listed on the minibar list and I thought that it was complimentary (and I was not the only one to think this) - it's not! So be careful as they will charge you and it is not that great and not worth the charge.The pool area is amazing and they have new furniture for the summer. A great spot to hang on, but lots of 'suits' walking around and lots of messing about with moving pool furniture around. The hotel is now managed by Ritz Carlton and I think the big boys in suits spend far to much time strutting around and getting in the way of the staff. The result - poor service levels as the team seems more worried about pleasing the managers and this means they spend less time on looking after those of us that pay.Lunch by the pool was awful. My starter and main arrived at the same time. My guest did not get her starter and then it arrived with her main! They only had one bottle of olive oil and balsalmic so they kept moving it from table to table - very poor for a five star hotel.Even in the restaurant the service was slow - 30 minutes for a starter.The spa is great. It was wonderful views and is worth a visit, BUT too many female staff keep coming in to the male area and this is very off putting for most male guests.Front Desk staff are very nice, but when I asked to leave my bags to have them put in the car (which, by the way, I ordered the Merc to collect me from the airport and take me back, so I was certainly spending the money!), they said I had to take it downstairs myself to the Bell team. I thought this was five star Ritz Carlton - I guess it is going down the four star route.I would return, but they need to improve their service for the prices they hope to command and if they want to have the Ritz Carlton service. Overall I am disappointed as there is nothing like Arts in Barcelona and they could do so much better.

I only stayed 2 nights  was tagging along with my husband who was at a conference.Room was wonderful. Very comfortable  great bathroom. <Content>Great Location, Beautiful Hotel The hotel at the time and may still be, the tallest building in Spain, well the neighboring Mapfri building is the same height. The location is unbeatable. It was nicer than many hotels / resorts community spa areas Dining, beaches, discotheques, all 15 floors down, and 50 yards from the front door. The concierges were extremely helpful, with any request. One of the best perks.My only gripe was the security / front desk people were rude (condescending) and disrespectful: We were constantly being challenged, as to what we were doing, what were our names, room number etc... We stood out, American, meager Spanish speaking weak mexican-spanglish at best, and dressed to casual country-club attire standards excluding my flip-flops (unless heading out on the town.) The point is We stood out so I expected them to learn my name, or recognize there is the American with the $12 flip-flops that has been here all week. Lobby staff, Um, excuse me, may I help you? Me, (continuing to walk towards the elevator) Sure, send up three ice cold aqua's con gas, no wait two con-gas, one no gas, gracias!, it's room 1520Overall a great hotel, I loved it, the slight disrespect aside, I still highly recommend it.

<Author>Scaggers
<Content>Wow! Stylish luxury by the sea I was lucky enough to stay at the Arts as part of a corporate weekend conference. From the outside the hotel is not particularly attractive, looking more like a high rise office block. However, once inside the stylish modern decor and rooms more than make up for it - I've never seen so many fresh flowers all in one place!. My room on the 10th floor was genuinely breathtaking. It was extremely spacious and the views were fantastic. The bathroom is out of this world with a separate shower room (complete with seat and multiple jets) which is like a mini wet room and mood lighting. The room is full of gadgets - automatic blinds, Bang  Oulsen TV and CD - it look a while to figure it all out. I didn't get to use many of the hotel facilities (gym, pool) as most of the weekend was planned by the conference organisers but the breakfast was great with plenty of choice. The hotel bar did seem a bit expensive but then we were drinking cocktails (and I guess the owners think if you can afford to stay here, then you can afford the bar bill)! My only niggle was that I had to ask 3 times before the batteries in my TV remote were changed but other the this the staff were very friendly and attentive. The hotel is well placed for sightseeing and nightlife (I think it is on the route of the hop on/hop off bus) and is right on the beach. Overall, it is probably the best hotel I have ever stayed in but if the price tag makes you feel faint, Hotel 1898 on Las Ramblas is very good at probably half the cost.

<Author>Shellfire
<Content>Very slick until the conference hordes arrive From the outside this hotel is distinctly underwhelming - one of a pair of high rise blocks that tower over the reclaimed coastline which passes for Barcelona's beach. It is, however, very slickly run from the multi-lingual smart young things that man the check-in desk to the porters, concierges and the room service staff. They are all charming and ready to deal promptly with any problems that arise of which there are, mercifully, few.We stayed up on the 17th floor having been told that it is a good idea to be high up in the building. I don't think it really matters - personally, I'd prefer to be looking straight out to sea rather than over the city but it may well be that a view over the towers and chimneys of Barcelona is more interesting. The bathroom was excellent, all the usual trappings but very well designed. There are plenty of buttons to press to alter the lighting, bring down the blinds, change channels - it's all quite high tech. I had breakfast in the room - very good, delicious pastries but, as ever, the 'fresh' orange juice wasn't fresh but they happily put that right, and the coffee was excellent. The pillows were good and there was a choice - what a relief.The only major downside was that if you happen to be staying when one of the large conferences decant their delegates, it can take forever to get into a lift. After a day slogging round the tourist spots when all you want to do is slip up to the room and get into a bath, it is infuriating to find you have to wait 25 minutes - and there is no alternative - you are not allowed to use a staircase, and grinding up 17 floors (which is only half way up the hotel) doesn't seem very appealing in any case. There is a good gym and the outdoor swimming pool is large, very well maintained with dozens of comfortable chairs around it and very attentive staff to bring towels, drinks etc.Barcelona is a wonderful city with a mass of things to see and do and I would definitely return.  
<Date>Dec 20, 2006

<Author>London,SW1
<Content>What a sad excuse for a hotel... This place is well past it. It may have cut it a few years back when Barcelona was one of the poorer European cities, but these days it has been left behind by a crop of much better and trendier places, actually located in town !A lump of concrete with some expensive shops does not equal a good hotel. Maybe in Baghdad I would accept this fake and soulless place and be happy that I was safe from bombs, but in central Barcelona (please note this hotel is nowhere near central), I have a choice of at least five better places.The hotel really needs to pick its act up as younger rich people are looking for more than over priced drinks, non-speaking Catalan staff and signage (Barcelona is the capital of Catalunya), and general drabness of this god awful place. The last time I went there I hoped I would never be unfortunate enough to return. I will remember this more clearly next time. Lastly, working girls may keep the (current roster of) business types happy, but the market has moved on, and it would be highly suggested to get out and look at some leading places such as : Malmaison, Hotel du Vin and Sofitel, which yes do charge your sort of high prices, but do deliver an exceptional service, not some drab pastiche of international travel that is no longer acceptable in 2006. I can only conclude that anyone who actually 'likes' this place has very little idea of what a leading venue should have to offer.

<Content>A very over-rated hotel The rooms and location of this hotel are excellent but our 3 night stay was spoilt by bad service:i) upon arrival our luggage was delivered to the wrong room and we did not receive it until 4 hours later; ii) sloppy room service - twice our room was not made up and towels not replenished, prompting more calls to manager in reception;iii) try leaving the hotel at peak time (8-9am and 6-7pm) and expect a 20 min wait on your floor for the lifts to arrive. Note we found you can take the fire exit stairs to the second floor and walk through a restaurant to get out but its a hassle, not least if you're on the 32nd floor!;iv) you actually need to take 2 separate lifts to leave the building and after 11pm you need to enter your key into a slot in the lift to make it work - nice security idea but would have been nice if staff`told us about it rather than finding out by chance!v) room minibar overpriced - e.g. 7 euros for a bottle of coke; they even charge for the tea  coffee vi) breakfast very average - hot courses consisted of scrambled egg, bacon, greasy potato and er, poached salmon?!? <Author>SteveP712
<Content>Fantastic hotel...if you avoid the pitfalls! The Arts is a cool, beautifully designed hotel with incredible rooms in a fantastic location...probably the only hotel in Barcelona directly on the beach. Although removed from the centre of the city, it is still an easy 20 minute walk or cheap 5 minute taxi ride to the main areas (Las Ramblas, Bari Gothic, etc.)HOWEVER, like any hotel it has its drawbacks, so be prepared to avoid/deal with the downsides to enjoy your stay.1. FOOD -- As other reviews noted, the prices in the hotel are absolutely ridiculous, even by 5 star standards. Go just outside the hotel to many of the fine restaurants along the beach and have a nice meal for the same price the Arts would charge you for a sandwich!!2. CONCIERGE -- Often a line, and the recommendations we received were either off the mark or outright wrong (stores they recommended were closed down or the address didn't exist). Buy a good guidebook, and only use the concierge to book or confirm reservations. 3. POOL -- Very nice, but very SMALL, especially for a 30 storey hotel. You might need to fight for a spot, or just head straight for the beach instead. Again, don't order too much from the poolside cafe, or you will pay the price (literally).4. ELEVATOR/LIFTS -- The one silly aspect of the hotel's design is that you much take 2 lifts every time you return to your room -- one to the lobby level and another from the lobby to your room.  
<Date>Sep 25, 2006

<Author>NYCWGV
<Content>Big, Sort of Coporate in Scale, but Great If you want a big cushy hotel on the beach, this is it. My partner and I opted out of staying at a boutique hotel in the heart of the city and we were so glad. This hotel was the most comfortable we ever stayed at with a fantastic room, great views, fast service, and a superb pool. From the door staff to the check in counter to the bartender , everyone was pleasant. The rooms are large and ours looked directly at the Sagrada Familia -- not bad! The location is great if one wants a beach/urban experience. Sitting by the pool feels like you're on the beach but look around and you can see that you're in a city with great architecture. If you are concerned about the location, there are always cabs that pull up to the front door that cost about $7 US dollars to get to the heart of Barcelona. It's well worth it given the quality of the hotel. But be aware, it's not small and due to its large towering size, can feel kind of corporate.

<Author>HoustonLawyer
<Content>Amazing room, Bad service The room is AMAZING. The view of the harbor, the ipod connected stereo system, the amazing shower, the comfy bed, the flatscreen tv, the electric window shades, etc, all means one word: SUPERCOOL. Even the hotel location is okay, because the tourist bus (the BEST way to get around the city) has a stop just outside the hotel. However, beware the service. If they could improve the service, this would be a top hotel even on a world-level standard. With the service as it is, it's worth the money, but only just.

<Author>1028
<Content>very good overall This is a very good hotel, but for the rates it charges it should be.We booked rooms on the Club floor, which although you pay more, do negate some of the issues about everything being very expensive once you get there. If you use the facilities, I think it represents good value.The rooms are very good and the service generally is excellent. <Author>lass=
<Content>Very Comfortable, Nice location for Summer Months We stayed at the Hotel Arts Barcelona in June for 4 nights with our two teenage daughters. We were extremely comfortable and thoroughly enjoyed our stay. Our rooms were very nicely appointed and on the large side. We had connecting rooms with a terrific sea view. We found the room cleaning staff to be exceptionally good. While the hotel pool is small, we never waited long for a lounge, and the pool side staff were terrific. We also enjoyed the miles of beach, for walking, lounging (local vendors rent chairs and umbrellas for the day) and terrific beach side restaurants. The food at the hotel was first rate, and not horribly priced, at least not in comparison to other 5-star hotels in Spain. We were pleased to find that the hotel offered an a la carte breakfast in addition to the buffet. Some days we just don't want to eat EURO 27 worth of food for breakfast. We also pleased that the hotel clientele came from differing nationalities. We had arrived at the hotel from a stay in Mallorca, where our hotel was occupied almost entirely by Brits. We found the greater range of nationalities of guests at Hotel Arts to make it more a more vibrant and happening environment. The hotel staff were very professional. Restaurant recommendations were generally very good. Service in restaurants was also good. On our first night at the hotel the noise from an outdoor wedding was loud until 3 am making it difficult to sleep. After a few phone calls to the night manager, who handled the calls very well, the hotel provided my husband and I with an additional room on the other side of the hotel less affected by the noise for the evening, and they removed the room charge for the night because of the inconvenience. Our original room was very quite for the rest of our stay. We used the gym facilities daily and found the gym to be well equipped. Our teenage daughters also greatly enjpyed our stay at the hotel. We would definitley return to Barcelona and to the Hotel Arts.

<Author>happydaysHerts
<Content>Outstanding hotel! A great option for families, with attentive staff, excellent food and a wonderful open-air pool - the biggest problem we had was tearing the girls away from the pool to go sightseeing! Be prepared for high prices: the room policy prevents a family of 4 sharing (although the girls' twin room had large queen beds and could have housed an army), thus escalating accomodation costs signficantly; no tea/coffee-making facilities resulting in 20 euros every time you want a cuppa; high bar/ restaurant prices. However, that's typically 5-star all over  doesn't take away from the fact that the Arts is a superb hotel, with outstanding standard bedrooms, bathrooms to get lost in  friendly staff. We had inter-connecting rooms, which worked very well. Girls (6  5) made to feel welcome - not simply tolerated. Hotel gets very busy during weekends, with ensuing lounger wars around the pool - weekdays much quieter. Buffet breakfast excellent (brand champagne included - go for it!). Close to some great seafood restaurants on the marina (Miravent gets our vote) and taxis into town very reasonably priced (takes about 10 mins). Could definitely see us going back!

<Author>bungo
<Content>Worth every penny On previous stays in Barcelona we've booked into Le Meridien on the Ramblas but this time thought I'd try the Hotel Arts - and am so pleased we did. The hotel just exudes comfort, cleanliness and style; even the lobby smells delicious!! Being by the sea - and with a gorgeous pool with double sunbeds and where you get attentive service (complimentary water, fruit, suncream etc)- it feels much more like a 'proper' holiday than being jammed into the city centre.The hotel is a good 40-minute walk from the Ramblas (don't let anyone tell you any different!)but the open-top tourist bus stops right outside the hotel which is pretty convenient for sightseeing.We paid for a deluxe sea-view room which was exactly what it claimed to be - beds were the comfiest I've known in a hotel too. Staff were considerably friendlier than in many luxury hotels and went out of their way to be helpful (not the supercilious look-down-their-nose at you types you often get in top hotels).Do try the Arola restaurant - we nearly didn't, thinking two Michelin stars would automatically mean second-mortgage prices, but it was quite the opposite. The starters are tapas-style (ie you choose a couple each and share) and were just gorgeous. Kids love nibbly things like that and, to their credit, even though Arola clearly likes to come across as funky (it has it's own DJ!) there were lots of families in there. Our 12-year-old thought it all very 'cool' and loved the food (result!)Only real drawback to the Hotel Arts are the breakfasts - the most eye-wateringly expensive I've seen yet. Ours wasn't included in the room rate we'd booked and there wasn't anywhere nearby that did anything more breakfasty than just coffee and a croissant. Also, we'd thought the seafood restaurants around Port Olimpic, just steps from the hotel, would be fantastic, but there are so many chasing the business we were 'hustled' as we walked along checking them out and ended up feeling quite uncomfortable (and the one we chose was rubbish!!) The following day we had lunch in a big seafood restaurant that virtually backs onto the hotel pool (can't remember the name, it was two words both beginning with M!), and had a fantastic lunch outside on their terrace, so would just go straight back there another time.I can't recommend the Hotel Arts highly enough. It really turned a city break weekend into something that felt like a laze-by-the-pool holiday too - the best of both worlds.  
<Date>Apr 11, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Absolutely the best After checking in to a different 5 star hotel,and being quite disappointed, we checked out and made our way to The Arts. The designation of 4/5 star hotels in Barcelona can be deceiving but The Arts is 6 stars. The personal attention, especially if your room includes the Club floor, is outstanding. The staff will do everything to please you. The rooms are spacious, beds and linens divine, and the views gorgeous. Bathrooms are beautiful and well appointed with fabulous rain showerheads as well as side jets. Whenever I called reception I was greeted by name and spoken to in English so I wonder if they make notes in their computer when you check in. This is a beautiful, service oriented hotel located just outside the hubub of the city but an easy taxi or tour bus ride into town. Great restaurants, the beach and a nice seaside promenade complete the picture. The Arts was the absolute best hotel I've ever stayed in and I am very picky!

<Author>misdirected_baggage
<Content>polished Absolutely perfect service. The staff at the front desk remembered my name from day one. Everyone was incredibly gracious to a fault. I upgraded to a corner, ocean view room (75 euro more) and it was worth every penny. I have stayed in luxury hotels around the world and this is one of my favorites. My traveling companion reserved a room on the private floors (special key entry) and the lounge for those floors serves an amazing tapas and wine buffet nightly. The hotel's restaurant is small, but the food is excellent with very attentive service. The breakfast buffet is also excellent. The only drawback to this hotel is that its location, though awsome for beach access, is inconvenient for walking tours and Barcelona taxis are (a) very expensive and (b) the drivers often tend to take one on the most roundabout route in order to run-up the meter.My only complaint is that the spa, although good, was not of the same calibre as the rest of the hotel. The venue was pretty, but it lacked towels, the hot tub was lukewarm, the sauna seemed to be cool and the treatments I had were OK, but not especially memorable. It's a beautiful spa situated at the top of the hotel and knowing the hotel arts, my experience was probably an off day.

<Author>Josug
<Content>Hotel Arts - worth it? Stayed at the Hotel Arts in January to celebrate out 10th wedding anniversary. We were pleased from the moment it started - all the staff smile and remember your name, but it is definitely worth paying more to stay on the executive floor. The club lounge is great with complimentary food and drink all day. We ended up spending more time there than anywhere else. The location is quite far out - not in the hubub of La Rambla but we preferred that as felt a bit nervous walking around the Barri Gotic at night. Everywhere was no more than a 10 euro taxi ride away and we also did a lot of walking, which is perfect when in Barcelona. We toyed between the boutique hotel experience such as Hotel Neri and having gone to see it when we were there, I am pleased we chose the Hotel Arts as the area felt safer and quieter. Hotel Neri is right next to a nursery backing onto a courtyard and it seemed very hustly and bustly. No complaints about Hotel Arts - everything was done quickly and without fuss and the staff were exceptionally helpful to us. We ate at the hotel restaurants, Bites was great - good food and not too expensive, Arola seems too hyped - the portions were small tapas style, but the staff seem to think they are the most important ones rather than the clients. It wasn't bad, just not as fantastic as it thinks it is. All in all, we were pleased with the Hotel Arts and think it was worth the money as it is expensive. By the way, there is free bottled water in the gym and spa which you can take rather than pay for it from the mini bar!

<Author>KateOK
<Content>Barcelona Arts--Urbane/hotcool My family of four,children are 11 and 14, stayed at the Arts for five days in late August. We travel quite a bit, but we had never been to this fabulous city.The hotel was unique. Our rooms, a two bedroom suite, with living room and a private connecting hallway, were just stunning. The positives were that we found it relaxing to look at the sea, and be away from the dancing, nightlife that went on into the wee hours of the night. It was quiet. We did not find it at all problematic to stay here, and not in the city-center.And the rooms were just serene. Well designed. The hotel staff were quick, bright, and tried to help all tourists. I did not feel, in August--of all times--as if my family was one of just many. I did feel as if the pool was over-run. Maybe hotels and resorts should begin to give numbers to lounge chairs, so that people don't feel possessed to wake at all hours and take up unoccupied space with their towels while they sleep/eat/tour.... is this becoming a world-wide flue of sorts???!@# The beach, right outside, is pretty common, open to all, very democratic. Which has its good bits and its tough parts. I would absolutely recommend this to those looking for the most contemporary of ammenities- slick, hospitable,sleek, urbane---and yet, you have easy access to the rest of the city. We thought it was white-cool. And Barcelona, well....go see it ! It is magnificent.KBoston

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Worth the money for the view alone Have just returned from a long weekend at the Hotel Arts Barcelona and it was absolutley amazing. We had an executive suite on the 33rd floor and the views of Barcelona and the marina to the other side were so breathtakingly wonderful, I could have sat and stared at them all weekend and have done nothing else! Yes, it is very expensive but this hotel is luxury personified. The staff are helpful and friendly without being snooty. If you can afford it, go for the Club Levels as the club lounge is a wonderfully relaxed place to hang out for breakfast or a drink before you head off for dinner.Our room had only been redecorated a month and was gorgeous, with luxurious lounge area and great sized bedroom. From both beds you get the amazing views so you can wake up, with a touch of a button have the shutters open and watch the city waking up.The bathroom is beautiful and the shower is like standing in Niagara Falls, to the extent I got a headache after a while!It is a bit of a walk to the Old Town, but still, you can amble through the park and then walk back along the sea (or get a taxi if you're feeling lazy) and therefore get to experience other parts of Barcelona that you may not have seen.All in all, I would not hesitate to recommend this to anyone (as long as you are not on a tight budget, or any sort of budget really!), particularly if you are going to Barcelona for a special treat as this hotel will do nothing but enhance it.
