<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Of course it's good, but it's not worth staying at Really good hotel, but that's to be expected at this price. The question is... is it worth it? And the answer is no. Why? Because...1. Location. Barcelona is not the place to go for great beaches. So why stay at the beach? You go there for the food, the gothic quarter, the architecture, the bars, the culture, and the vibe. Staying out here alienates you from most of that (unless the pinnacle of your Barcelona visit is to be a night out at the Baja Beach Club in which case ignore everything I say). 2. The rooms. I think the rooms are in the process of renovation. And they really do need it. 2006 may well be a better year to visit than 2005, when the rooms may well have reached their post-opening (1992) nadir. 3. The pool. Tiny, over-busy, full of kids. Not enough sun loungers by a mile. 4. The cost. Not just of the rooms, but of the million and one overpriced extras that are the hallmark of luxury American chain hotels. As a result, the prevailing feeling all around is of money, not style or class. 5. The alternatives. Hotel Neri for example is fabulous and captures the essence of Barcelona perfectly. On the plus side, the hotel is still clearly very, very good. The views from the higher floors are pretty spectacular. Food at Arola is excellent. Agua restaurant on the beach is a great place for Sunday lunch. And Restaruant Barceloneta in nearby (and walkable) Barceloneta is probably the best seafood place in town. I wouldn't go back, but I'm still happy enough that I went, if you know what I mean.

<Author>torta_basilica
<Content>Better Than Expected... Luckily, our hopes were not up after reading all of the reviews, but it's not like there's one stellar hotel in Barcelona that stands heads  shoulders above the others... I didn't mind the location - could still walk or taxi everywhere. Our room on the 9th floor had a great view of the Olympic port  was quite nice. Everything worked  I felt lucky! Had a few issues with room service, but it was always friendly, if slow  expensive. Staff were great  very friendly. Bathroom was well-equipped - very nice marble shower - I didn't like the shower door-type closing on the toilet/bidet area, though - this could have been done better. Plenty of closet  storage space  the built-in desk/office area was very efficient  effective. Was nice not to have my husband's computer  work stuff spread all over the room for once! The pool area is beautiful  I had no problems booking at manicure at their associated Beauty Center. Only complaint would be that the gift shop is really weak on things you actually might need while travelling  the public carpets are badly in need of a thorough cleaning or replacement. Other than that, we had a great stay.BTW, when you totally burn out on tapas, there's a good little Italian restaurant in the Olympic port - al Passatore - very casual, but I had Linguine al Cartoccio - incredible seafood linguine delivered in a swan shaped foil packet. The caprese salad was weak, but this pasta was to die for!!

<Author>stlm
<Content>Great Experience I stayed at the Hotel Arts on my Honeymoon from May 13th until May 15th, before my Mediterranean Cruise.Our rate was $335 EUR per night, buffett breakfast included and it was WORTH IT!!We got a room on the 23rd floor with views of the Mediterranean Sea and the city, since it was our first time in Barcelona, the Bellman suggested to take the Tourist Bus, which has a stop in the corner of the hotel (Great way to see the city), the bus stops at different monuments and landmarks of barcelona and you can hop on and off whenever you like. There are 3 bus lines, and the Arts stop is the connecting stop for the Blue and Green Lines.Anyway, when we arrived at the room, they had a bottle of Spanish Cava (Sparkling Wine), a plate with chocolate covered strawberries, a heart made of rose petals on the bed and candles all over the place, we didn麓t ask for it (I asked my husband if he麓d ordered it) and it was a nice detail from the hotel.The room is HUGE, the bed very comfortable, you can control all the lights and drapes from your night stand and huge closets.The bathroom was all marble separate shower and tub, two sinks, and all the amenities you need.Service was TOP NOTCH, the concierge very helpful, made reservation for Dinner at a nice restaurant in Barcelona, and the next day suggested a Tapas Bar. Actually we got robbed on our second day in Barcelona, and we had to report all my husband麓s credit cards, and they were extremly helpful, even they helped me to file a police report, and gave me some water and chocolates to calm down.My overall experience is EXCELLENT hotel, yes the location isn麓t the best but the Tousrit Bus and the cabs are just outside, I will definetly stay ther my next time in Barcelona.

<Author>Transatlanticgirl
<Content>Posh but you pay the price Hotel Arts is a posh hotel with posh prices and if that is what you want then fine. Rooms are very spacious, clean and the service was excellent (except in the restaurant which is extremely expensive for what you get). I stayed on business and that's the only way I would stay here. It's fine for business meetings and the like but for tourists, it's a way from the town centre (10/15 mins in a cab). If you want better value and a central location then stay in town. I've stayed in the NH Duc de la Victoria - which is not in the same league as the Arts being a 3 star (but a very good 3 star at that - should be 4*) but it's less than half the price of the Hotel Arts and much more in the middle of things for those who want to be tourists and see this wonderful city.The open top tourist buses are great value and cover pretty much everything you'd want to see and you can get on and off during the 12 hours they run. They do stop near the Hotel Arts as alternative way of getting into town. A bargain at 17 Euros for one day and 21 Euros for 2 consecutive days!

<Author>Petizza
<Content>What Wow Factor? We spent 3 days there in 2004. Our trip started with a bad omen as our luggage had disapeared on Iberia flight from Madrid. The staff did not seem very sympathetic. I constantly had to call Iberia (thank goodness I speak spanish fluently) because the staff was not offering much help other that we will send your bags up when they get here After 2 days and about 20 calls later my bags were found in Athens and were returned the day before we had to leave.  Anyway as this is not a review about Iberia, I really feel that the Hotel should have done more to help us deal with the situation. I had to ask them where we could get toiltetires, clothes etc. None of this assistance was offered even though they told me that this is a common occurence. I found the hotel decor dated. It was not a Boutique hotel like the ones in U.S say like the Schrager Hotels. There were some minimalist features but it was sort of a mix between minimalism and gaudy (think lots of pink marble) The rooms are carpeted and our room had a pink/peach hue, more pink marble in the bathroom. We also did not enjoy the white flourescent lights by the windows, which might give a cool aspect from outside the building but not very nice on the inside. And for those people saying that the location is not bad, it is bad. To have to take a 5 min taxi ride or to have to take a taxi ride everywhere you go is not good in my book. It reminded me to living in Battery Park City in New York, where Tribeca and Soho are so close but not really. I enjoy walking in cities and the walk between the hotel and anywhere else in not nice. If you were staying in the center of town you could have a nice walk in any number of directions. If you are going to spend the money I recommend you stay in one of the hotels in the center of town. The choice is very much like the difference between Battery Park City and Soho, where would you rather be?

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved the Hotel Arts. I stayed at the hotel arts Feb. 18 - 21st.All I can say is, if you are going to Barcelona, this is the place to be.The hotel is absolutely stunning. fresh flowers everywhere, a fantastic staffand the location is amazing. Right on the beach with great restaurants all around it. Bestial is a lot of fun and Abac is not to be missed. If you stay in a club suite (and you should) the club lounge is better than most of the restaurants in Barcelona. The pool and sculpture garden are a nice touch.All in all the time we spent at The Hotel Arts was actually the best time we had in Barcelona. I would put this hotel in a class with the Ritz Carlton in New York and the Morrison in Dublin. Truly a great hotel. I read a number of reviews that referred to the location as a negative. I couldn't disagree more. Barcelona is much prettier from the 32nd floor of this hotel then it is from street level. The area around the hotel is actually the nicest part of Barcelona and you can hail a cab or walk about 50 yards to the subway station and go anywhere you want in a few minutes. Aword of warning about the cab drivers in Barcelona - every other one of them will rip you off in ever imaginative ways. Be aware and be careful. the subway was great by the way.

<Author>LondonShoegal
<Content>Worth a visit for the views alone We'd booked The Hotel Arts because we wanted to stay somewhere nice. We weren't expecting palatial treatment as we'd booked a late, special offer online... wow! From the moment we arrived, we couldn#t have been treated better. Concierge so helpful (where you spoke Spanish or not) that you wanted to take them home with you. Reception upgraded us on arrival to a corner club room with breathtaking views - over the sea, the port olympic and into town. Beds so comfortable and luxurious bathrooms with separate shower, bath and toilet - a rarity when most hotels squeeze the space away.The location wasn't an issue - apart from the fact that there was no real options directly outside the hotel - but you're not visiting a resort but a city! The tour buses stop right outside the hotel, taxis are abundant AND you don't get all the noise from the late night revellers if you want to get a good night's sleep. All in all, was expecting an average visit to a luxurious hotel (had booked Hotel Majestic, but cancelled having read the reviews here!) and couldn't have asked for a better visit.!Viva espana!

<Author>dannycarlucci
<Content>Enjoyed my stay at the Hotel Arts I stayed at the Hotel Arts for a business conference at the beginning of March 2005. The hotel is very nice. The decor of the public areas is modern looking - more like a W than a Ritz Carlton. The staff is very nice and helpful and just about everyone spoke English - particularly the front desk staff and concierge. The staff was helpful in giving directions, recommending activities, and they arranged an 5:00 A.M. taxi to the airport. The location of the hotel is away from the main tourist area, but only a short cab ride away. If you are in decent shape, you can walk to La Rambla in about 20 minutes. I would imagine that during the summer the location is very attractive, being right on the beach. Unfortuantely, it was very cold during my stay (it even snowed one day). The rooms were very nice. I stayed in a regular room which was extremely large by European standard. However, it did take me a while to figure out the light switches and, even with all of the room lights on, it seemed dark in the room. The rooms could use a little sprucing up. The rug looked like it was a bit ragged. However, all in all, I would say that the Hotel Arts is a wonderful hotel and would not hesitate to recommend staying here.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Could do just a little bit better I stay in hotels for over 100 days a year, so know what to expect. I use the Ritz Carlton hotels in the US and Four Seasons hotels in Europe, so I also know what a good top end hotel should be. Many friends had stayed at the Arts and came back with rave reviews, so I had very high expectations.Yes it is a great hotel. Forget those saying how far it is from the tourist centre of town, its only a 5 min taxi ride, and the peaceful marina location is great to come back to after a hard day at work/play.The public spaces are lovely with great design and they have a great 'wow' factor. I had a suite on the 23rd floor, which was very large, with wonderful views, so it should have been perfect, but.....The fittings in the room, other than the hi tech, which is very good, are all looking a little tired. Some lights were broken, a lamp shade was ripped, the bathrooms are 10 years out of date. My shower pressure was also a little limp. The carpets are looking a little worse for wear, and there are the creeping signs of neglect around the edges. At a regualr Ritz Carlton its the attention to detail that makes them the premier hotel group in the world, and its a shame that the management here, don't seem to go for detail.The staff were great, and very attentive, but room service was a little slow and as others have reported, calling the front desk is a challange. That said, the service from the the conciege was excellent.I would recommend, rather than rave about this place. If they renovated the bathrooms, replaced a few light bulbs and just gave the rooms a fresh makeover, there would be few hotels in Spain to compete with these guys.

<Author>malser
<Content>Well-Done Stayed here on the last leg of our honeymoon in August 2003 and loved it. The hotel somehow manages to be modern yet warm and comfortable at the same time. After staying at older more European-style hotels in other parts of Spain, it was a pleasure to get to the clean, comfy elegance of the Arts. The rooms are comfortable and outfitted with Bang  Olufsen stereos and bedside controls for the window shades and lights. The shower is possibly the greatest hotel shower on earth- large with multiple showerheads that spray you from top to bottom. We were upgraded to club level so were on a high floor, with amazing views of the city, and had access to the club lounge, which was a nice addition. The pool area is great but crowded. The staff is warm and friendly. My only complaint is the location. The Porto Olympico area is nice but it would be nice to be within walking distance of Las Ramblas or Passeig de Gracia. Inevitably you'll take cabs or the Metro downtown- it's only a 5-minute ride. There are a few great restaurants on the beach (Aqua) but otherwise a dearth of good food outside the hotel. Still, I think it's worth it to stay here, a tad outside of downtown- the hotel is that good.

<Author>kingdom100
<Content>Service is a fine art at Hotel Arts Upon my arrival, the bell captain swiftly removed the luggage from the taxi and whisked it away. One enters a small lobby with two sofas, and a wonderful French delicatessen, 鈥淗ediard鈥? Two lifts lead into the main lobby of the hotel. The reception area is stylish, if a little bland and international, a frosted glass chandelier looking most out of place. Receptionist was swift and efficient, and obliged my request for a sea view room (having only reserved a city view) on a high floor. To access the rooms, one leaves the lobby down a passageway which has various vases and cut flowers decorating it, to yet another lobby housing the six lifts. Lifts are lined in a burr wood, with the only mirrors being the doors. The corridors leading to the bedrooms are a little bland, lifted only by the occasional painting. The bedroom comprised a small lobby with two double (single hanging) wardrobes, which led into a very long, but rather narrow room with a marvellous 鈥渨ide screen鈥?picture window with views over the pool, marina, and ocean beyond. The bathroom, to my surprise, felt rather dated, with peachy cream sanitary-ware. No Bulgari toiletries (as noted in other reviews), but ones created 鈥渆xclusively for Hotel Arts鈥?by some squiggled signatured company in 鈥淗ong Kong and New York鈥? That said, they were of a relatively good standard. The bathtub was long and wide, but took a terribly long time to fill to a suitable depth. A toilet and bidet were contained in a screened off area, as was the shower cubicle. Unfortunately, as I was to discover, the seal on the shower door wasn鈥檛 as flush/tight as it should have been. The combination of two side jets and one fixed head led to one finding the entire bathroom flooded upon exiting the shower. I wondered whether, perhaps, I had left the door slightly ajar, however, when the bathroom was flooded yet again on the next day, I realised it was the seal at fault. The staff were very quick in mopping up the soaking floor, and replacing the towels that I had used in an effort to dry the floor. The bed was comfortable, but still had old fashioned sheets, not a more modern duvet. The control panel (for speakers, blind, and lights) beside the bed which incorporated an alarm clock was a very well thought out feature. One could wake up and at the touch of a button be greeted by ocean views! The Bang  Olufsen stereo was sadly not supplemented by speakers of comparable quantity, those provided were a little feeble and lacking depth of sound - a shame to waste such a great system on them. The television was a little awkwardly placed if one had wanted to watch it in bed. No video library rendered the thoughtfully provided VCR useless - does one really travel with video cassettes? DVDs perhaps, but not videos! A previous reviewer had commented on the 鈥渃heap鈥?fitted furniture. In fact, it is cleverly designed laminated furniture so as to blend in with the wallpaper, and not become a feature in itself. All cupboards were well lit. An iron was provided in the room, along with an ironing board, something I find a little strange for a deluxe property. There were other American school touches like this throughout the entire hotel, nothing wrong, just a little out of place.The gardens were small, but well landscaped and incorporating terraces for bars, restaurants and a pool deck. The pool was ludicrously small for such a large property, the sun loungers started to free up in the late afternoon. Pool staff did not speak English of any standard - they did not understand when asked for 鈥渢owels鈥?even when coupled with a drying gesture. Loungers were available in single or double sizes, and some had 鈥渢ents鈥?enveloping them, presumably for those who prefer the shade. Complimentary bottles of chilled water, and apples were available, and even sun lotion and champagne at extra cost. The lobby area behind the reception contained a small lounging area filled with sofas, deep seated leather chairs and a selection of coffee table books about fashion, architecture and travel. Lemon and minted water was provided in large jugs in the centre of this room. Off of here was the 鈥淏ites鈥?restaurant - a small menu, with lighter dishes that sounded very sickly. On the opposite side was a breakfast room cum lounge, containing more low sofas and deep chairs. A gas fire burnt night and day to serve as a focal point. In the summer this seems ridiculous, style for style鈥檚 sake, some function and logic would have been much appreciated. This room led into the bar, a small room with yet more low chairs and banquettes decorated with black and white photography of the Marx brothers. A small 鈥渨alk-in鈥?humidor in one corner with the bar running along the length of the room. Drinks were steeply, and irregularly priced. A mojito (well made, and a generous size) was priced the same as a champagne cocktail at 16EUR - fine for the latter, but too much for the former. Martinis were all 13EUR. It seemed as if they had been rather lazy and thoughtless in pricing the drinks, almost with the attitude 鈥渋f you can afford to stay here, anything goes鈥? Service was prompt and efficient. I will note that the cigars were all cheaper than if shop bought in the UK, but I imagine this is something more to do with duty/taxes rather than the hotel鈥檚 generosity.The restaurant where one took a buffet breakfast (the name has recently changed and is no longer that advertised in the room) had a large terrace with equally large and cumbersome pieces of wooden furniture. Service, as in the bar, was prompt and efficient, copious amounts of fresh orange juice, and good quality (but by no means the best) coffee was offered by waitresses who continually swanned around. The buffet itself has the usual breads, fruits and pastries. Most notable were the bagels (another American touch), Moet et Chandon champagne, and fresh strawberries with cream that were provided. 25EUR + 7% tax seems relatively good value when compared to other dining options at this property. I took breakfast on three out of five mornings, whilst it is not the best hotel breakfast I鈥檝e had, it is one of the best, certainly recommended. I should also point out that 鈥淏ites鈥?offers an 脿 la carte breakfast menu, but after one would鈥檝e ordered orange juice and coffee, it is more cost effective to have had the buffet and had only a few things.Arola had an excellent menu, however, on the evening I had decided to try it, I was informed (in the morning) that it was fully booked. If I had known it would be so popular I would鈥檝e booked it upon my arrival, I feel that the receptionist should have not overlooked this when checking me into the hotel, at the very least there should be a note in the room advising very early booking. Instead I dined at the main restaurant (Enoteca Bombasti - or words to that effect!). Again I noted the weird pricing system. Starters ranged in price from 10EUR-28EUR (excluding caviar), and main/fish courses from 18-32EUR. The starters seem overpriced, and the main courses slightly underpriced, this is inconsequential, but looks strange on the menu. Food was well presented, if a little sickly at times, but all in all, an enjoyable meal. The poolside restaurant was very casual, and offered a light menu, pizzas, grilled meats, and suchlike; it was also of an equally high standard, with efficient and courteous service. I did not take any other meals at the hotel, but it all seemed to be pretty international fare.Service was very American styled: 鈥淚t is my pleasure, have a nice day鈥? which was polite, if rather insincere, but this cannot really be criticised. The concierge was excellent, pointing out various places of interest and locating them on a map, as well as shopping suggestions - they cannot be blamed for Barcelona鈥檚 lack of quality shopping. When I requested the room to be serviced within the hour, they obliged, with smiles on their faces.As a last note, the hotel lacked atmosphere, this was due to the guests staying there. Mainly brash Britons from Essex (read Louis Vuitton obsessives), and various sections of American society; ranging from older people 鈥渙n vacation鈥?to terribly green corporate types; one man asked his colleague, after touching his trousers 鈥渁re they wool鈥?followed by, 鈥渁m I dressed okay?鈥? how green! During the day people walked around the lobby in sandals, and shorts, which is acceptable given the casual and resort nature of the hotel. However, at 11PM I do not expect to see people walking barefoot (mainly Americans I am afraid) though the hotel. There was no grand or even stylish atmosphere, the hotel had a rather too corporate emphasis on things. If I were to return to the city (which I won鈥檛 be) I would stay there again as it was such a relief to escape the madness of the city centre and walk along the pleasant (if corpse like) beach.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Luxury hotel for families! I've just got back from spending Easter at the Hotel Arts! The hotel service is absolutely superb and its design ( exterior and interior) is breathtaking.I had an amazing huge room with 2 double beds and a view of the marina, beach and city ( and that was just a standard family room). Hotel even has an amazing outdoor pool and jacuzzi on the second floor where you could just chill out all day. Hotel is just a short walk from shops and restaurants on the marina and a 5 minute walk to the Zoo ( recommend hiring green electric car at the zoo- 13 euros for 1 hour for 2 adults and 2 kids- fantastic way to see the zoo!). Port Vell also 5 minutes by taxi ( about 8 euros) is nearby with a mini- fairground for children. There is a taxi stand just outside the hotel entrance and the metro is about a 5 minute walk away. The Barcelona tourist ' turisme' bus also leaves from just outside the hotel. I would highly recommend this hotel especially to those with children. I viewed the other Hotels in Barcelona and none compared to the Arts in relation to location, style and overall class! Only disadvantage- no kids tv channel but can bring own VHS video tapes as room has video player.

The hotel offers some of the most splendid views over the 1992 Olympic marina and the Northern Mediterranean. The lobby of the hotel is spectacular. The hotel runs with absolubt fluency and offers the most excuisit choise of breakfast. The rooms are very comfortable, and provides the visitor with every thing they require and more. This is simply the most spectacular and luxurious hotel in Barcelona.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Top of The Line Just returned from a short trip to Europe, which included a two-night stay at the Hotel Arts. The limited amount of service we were exposed to was quite good and we waited little more than a few minutes to have the few requests we made fully satisfied. The rooms are fantastic and extremely large, even by US standards. We had booked a special rate that was substantially under rack and still had a large, extremely well appointed room with a view of the Marina. The marble bathrooms are huge with separate showers and a deep tub. The beds are extremely comfortable with high quality bedding. We enjoyed the Bang  Olufsen stereo while unwinding after a day of touring. Our short stay did not allow us time to use the spa and the pool was closed for winter but both looked wonderful.I was a bit apprehensive about the location, as the hotel is not located in the heart of the city. It turned out that the old city it is within a ten-minute walk, the metro is nearby and there are inexpensive taxis lined up out front of the hotel at most hours. There are plenty of decent restaurants within a few blocks of the hotel and the beach is right out front. All in all, it was an excellent stay and one I wouldn?t mind repeating in the near future. Next time I?ll stay a bit longer and enjoy some of what the hotel has to offer.
